Non-coding RNAs were predicted by the Infernal program using default parameters<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           29, 2933â2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2635">52</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec12">Phylogenetic tree and genomic synteny</h3><p>We identified paralogs and orthologs using OrthoMCL v1.4 with the default settings (BLASTP E-valueââ¤â1e-5 and MCL inflation parameter of 1.5)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. &#xA;                           13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2647">53</a></sup>. The protein sequence sets from six sequenced plants (<i>B. distachyon</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>S. bicolor</i>, <i>S. italica</i>, <i>Z. mays</i>, <i>A. thaliana</i>; Phytozome v9.0) and <i>E. crus-galli</i> were used to perform gene family identification. The protein sequences of single-copy genes among the seven species identified by OrthoMCL were aligned using MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Katoh, K., Misawa, K., Kuma, K. i. &amp; Miyata, T. MAFFT: a novel method for rapid multiple sequence alignment based on fast Fourier transform. Nucleic Acids Res. &#xA;                           30, 3059â3066 (2002)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2673">54</a></sup>. After the Gblocks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Castresana, J. Selection of conserved blocks from multiple alignments for their use in phylogenetic analysis. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           17, 540â552 (2000)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2677">55</a></sup> alignment optimization, single-copy genes with aligned protein sequences longer than 1000 amino acids (aa) were chosen for phylogenetic tree construction and divergence time estimation. Species divergence times were estimated using an uncorrelated relaxed clock in BEAST v1.7.5 with <i>A. thaliana</i> as an outgroup<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Drummond, A. J., Suchard, M. A., Xie, D. &amp; Rambaut, A. Bayesian phylogenetics with BEAUti and the BEAST 1.7. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           29, 1969â1973 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2685">56</a></sup>. Monophyletic constraints were imposed for the nodes that were used to calibrate the evolutionary rates (Blosum62 and an uncorrelated exponential relaxed model). We used a Yule speciation process, which specifies a constant rate of species divergence. Normal priors were used for monocot-dicot split time (mean: 150.0 Mya, std dev: 4.0) and for <i>O. sativa</i>-<i>Z. mays</i> split time (mean: 50.0 Mya, std dev: 4.0). The MCMC chains in BEAST were run for 10,000,000 generation sampling every 1,000 steps. Convergence between the runs and the amount of burn-in (throwing away some iterations at the beginning of an MCMC run) was determined using Tracer v1.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Rambaut, A. &amp; Drummond, A. J. Tracer v1.5. &#xA;                    http://beast.bio.ed.ac.uk/Tracer&#xA;                    &#xA;                   (2009)" href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2695">57</a></sup>, which was used to assess the effective sample size and to check the consistency of the results. The tree was drawn with FigTree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Rambaut, A. FigTree 1.3, &#xA;                    http://tree.bio.ed.ac.uk/software/figtree/&#xA;                    &#xA;                   (2009)" href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2699">58</a></sup>. For genomic synteny, we first used BLASTP (E-valueââ¤â10-7) to align the <i>E. crus-galli</i> protein dataset to that of <i>S. bicolor</i>, <i>S. italica</i> and itself. The alignments were then subjected to DAGchainer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Haas, B. J., Delcher, A. L., Wortman, J. R. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. DAGchainer: a tool for mining segmental genome duplications and synteny. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           20, 3643â3646 (2004)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2713">59</a></sup> to determine syntenic blocks. The 4dTv of each syntenic block was calculated by an in-house Perl script.</p><p>To build phylogenetic trees for the genes of momilactone A gene clusters, ten grass species (including <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>O. punctata</i>, <i>O. brachyantha</i>, <i>Zizania latifolia</i>, <i>Brachypodium distachyon</i>, <i>S. bicolor</i>, <i>Z. mays</i>, <i>Panicum virgatum</i>, and <i>Setaria italic, E. crus-galli</i>) were involved and <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> was used as outgroup. BLASTP was used to scan homologous genes to rice genes of the cluster in the protein dataset (E-value thresholds: MAS: 1e-80; KSL4, CPS4, and CYP99A2: 1e-100). Raxml v8<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics. &#xA;                           30, 1312â1313 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2751">60</a></sup> was applied with the parameters â-m PROTGAMMAAUTO âauto-protâ=âbicâ to automatically select the best protein model for tree construction<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics. &#xA;                           30, 1312â1313 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2756">60</a></sup>. Each tree was constructed with 100 bootstraps.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">Investigations for P450 and GST</h3><p>Members of the CYP450 (PF00067) and GST (PF13417, PF13410, PF13409, PF00043, and PF02798) gene families were identified by InterProScan v5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Zdobnov, E. M. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterProScanâan integration platform for the signature-recognition methods in InterPro. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           17, 847â848 (2001)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2768">51</a></sup>. The phylogenetic tree was constructed by Fasttree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Price, M. N., Dehal, P. S. &amp; Arkin, A. P. FastTree: computing large minimum evolution trees with profiles instead of a distance matrix. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           26, 1641â1650 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2772">61</a></sup> with protein sequence alignments by MAFFT v7.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Katoh, K., Misawa, K., Kuma, K. i. &amp; Miyata, T. MAFFT: a novel method for rapid multiple sequence alignment based on fast Fourier transform. Nucleic Acids Res. &#xA;                           30, 3059â3066 (2002)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2776">54</a></sup>. For divergence estimation of <i>CYP450</i> and <i>GST</i> genes, phylogenetic trees of <i>CYP450</i> and <i>GST</i> genes in <i>E. crus-galli</i> and <i>O. sativa</i> were constructed by Fasttree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Price, M. N., Dehal, P. S. &amp; Arkin, A. P. FastTree: computing large minimum evolution trees with profiles instead of a distance matrix. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           26, 1641â1650 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2799">61</a></sup> with an Arabidopsis gene (<i>CYP450</i>: AT1G75130.1; <i>GST</i>: AT1G59670.1) as outgroup, respectively. The substitution distances are measured by MEGA v5.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Tamura, K. et al. MEGA5: Molecular evolutionary genetics analysis using maximum likelihood, evolutionary distance, and maximum parsimony methods. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           28, 2731â2739 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2810">62</a></sup>. On the basis of identified Pfam information for all genes of five grass species (<i>O. sativa</i>, <i>B. distachyon</i>, <i>S. bicolor</i>, <i>S. italica</i>, <i>Z. mays</i>) and <i>E. crus-galli</i> based on InterProScan v5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Zdobnov, E. M. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterProScanâan integration platform for the signature-recognition methods in InterPro. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           17, 847â848 (2001)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2833">51</a></sup>, enrichment analysis was conducted to examine whether <i>CYP450</i> and <i>GST</i> genes are over-presented in the <i>E. crus-galli</i> genome by hypergeometric test.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Genomic and transcriptomic investigations for allelopathy</h3><p>We searched barnyardgrass orthologs in known biosynthesis gene clusters<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Boycheva, S., Daviet, L., Wolfender, J. &amp; Fitzpatrick, T. B. The rise of operon-like gene clusters in plants. Trends Plant. Sci. &#xA;                           19, 447â459 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2855">15</a></sup> to identify candidate gene clusters in the <i>E. crus-galli</i> genome that are involved in the allelopathic interaction.</p><p>The relay seeding in agar (RSA) method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Navarez, D. &amp; Olofsdotter, M. (ed. Brown, H.) Proceedings of 1996 Second International Weed Control Congress 1285â1290 (Copenhagen, Denmark: DJF Flakkebjerg, 1996)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2865">63</a></sup> with a few modifications was used to investigate the allelopathic interactions between barnyardgrass (STB08) and rice (PI312777). Ten germinated PI312777 seeds were first transferred to a plastic tissue culture box (10âcm in base diameter) filled with 50âml of medium containing 0.5% agar, and arranged in three rows with a 3-4-3 pattern (Supplementary Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#MOESM1">5</a>). Germinated STB08 seeds were first transferred to a Petri dish with sterile water. Five days later, 10 germinated STB08 seeds were transferred to the tissue culture box containing germinated PI312777 seeds with a pattern of five STB08 seeds between two rows of PI312777 seeds (Supplementary Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#MOESM1">5</a>). The PI312777 and STB08 seedlings were co-cultured in a SAFE incubator (Ningbo, China) kept at 75% relative humidity. Mono-cultured STB08 seedlings (i.e., seedlings growing alone, under the same conditions) were used as controls. The entire co- and mono-cultured STB08 seedlings were collected at 3âh and RNA extracted for RNA-Seq analysis. A total of three biological replicates were collected for each condition.</p><p>Illumina RNA-Seq libraries were prepared and sequenced on a HiSeq4000 system following the manufacturerâs instructions. The raw paired-end reads were first filtered into clean data using NGSQCtookit v2.3.3 with default settings<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Patel, R. K. &amp; Jain, M. NGS QC Toolkit: a toolkit for quality control of next generation sequencing data. PLoS ONE &#xA;                           7, e30619 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2878">64</a></sup>. The cleaned reads were then aligned to the <i>E. crus-galli</i> genome assembly using Tophat v2.0.9<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Trapnell, C., Pachter, L. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNAâSeq. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           25, 1105â1111 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2885">65</a></sup>. After alignment, the count of mapped reads from each sample was derived and normalized to fragments per kilobase of exon per million fragments mapped for each predicted transcript using the Cufflinks package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNAâseq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat. Biotechnol. &#xA;                           28, 511â515 (2010)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2889">66</a></sup>. The resulting alignment files were then supplied to Cuffdiff in the Cufflinks package for differential expression analysis.</p><p>The allelopathic transcriptomic profile of our experiment was investigated using the Mapman software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Thimm, O. et al. MAPMAN: A user-driven tool to display genomics data sets onto diagrams of metabolic pathways and other biological processes. Plant. J. &#xA;                           37, 914â939 (2004)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2896">67</a></sup>. All <i>E. crus-galli</i> genes were first submitted to the online functional annotation sever called Mercator<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Lohse, M. et al. Mercator: a fast and simple web server for genome scale functional annotation of plant sequence data. Plant. Cell Environ. &#xA;                           37, 1250â1258 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2903">68</a></sup>. The log2 ratio of fold change (co-culture/mono-culture) was calculated for each significantly differentially expressed gene. The resulting files were loaded into Mapman to visualize the transcriptomic profile and perform the pathway enrichment study.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Experiments for DIMBOA measurement</h3><p>For DIMBOA measurement, mono- (six plants in a tissue culture box) or co-cultivated (three <i>Echinochloa</i> and three rice plants in a box) hydroponic <i>Echinochloa</i> weeds (STB08) and rice (PI312777) seedlings at the first-leaf stage were transplanted to deionized water for 45âmin, 1.5 and 3âh. Both mono- and co-cultivated <i>Echinochloa</i> and rice plants (whole plant) were then analyzed by HPLC after freeze-drying.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Experiments for <i>P. oryzae</i> infection</h3><p>
                           <i>Pyricularia oryzae</i> strains were cultured on agar plates containing complete medium for 10 days and conidia were harvested and re-suspended in 0.2% (w/v) gelatin solution. About 10<sup>5</sup> conidia per ml were sprayed evenly onto <i>E. crus-galli</i> plants at the three-leaf stage using an artistâs airbrush (Badger Co., Illinois) with the 0.2% (w/v) gelatin solution as control<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Su, Z. Z. et al. Evidence for biotrophic lifestyle and biocontrol potential of dark septate endophyte harpophora oryzae to rice blast disease. PLoS ONE &#xA;                           8, e61332 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d12320e2944">69</a></sup>. The inoculated plants were placed in a dew chamber at 22âÂ°C for 48âh in the dark and then transferred in a growth chamber under a photoperiod of 12âh for 7 days. Leaves with lesion was used for examination of gene expression by qRT-PCR. The relative value for the expression level of <i>MAS</i> and <i>KSL4</i> genes was calculated by the <span class="mathjax-tex">\({2^{ - \Delta \Delta {C_{\rm{T}}}}}\)</span> method using the Tubulin gene as an internal control. Primers for qRT-PCR were given in Supplementary TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5#MOESM1">7</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Data availability</h3><p>All raw DNA sequencing reads (Illumina and PacBio data) for <i>E. crus-galli de novo</i> assembly, sequencing data for <i>E. oryzicola</i>, and RNA-Seq data for the gene prediction and allelopathic experiments have been deposited under NCBI BioProject PRJNA268892. The SRA accession numbers are SRR5920284-SRR5920293, SRR5902661, SRR5903813-SRR5903830, and SRR5903559-SRR5903564. The <i>E. crus-galli</i> genome assembly and the annotated genes are accessible at <a href="http://ibi.zju.edu.cn/RiceWeedomes/Echinochloa/">http://ibi.zju.edu.cn/RiceWeedomes/Echinochloa/</a>, and the assembly is also available at ENA (European Nucleotide Archive) under assembly accession GCA_900205405. All relevant data contained within the paper are available from the corresponding author on request.</p></div></div></section>

H.Y., D.-S.K., D.A., L.G., Y.-Y.W., G.L., F.F., C.L., Q.S., C.-Y.Y. and L.F. collected and identified the <i>Echinochloa</i> species. J.Q., G.J., H.Z., Y.-F.W. and W.S. sequenced and assembled the genomes. J.Q., G.J., L.M., H.Z., L.J., Z.L., L.C., E.S., W.W., Q.C., D.W., S.W., Q.P., Y.Z., X.Z., L.W., L.W. and C.-Y.Y. performed sequence analysis. C.-H.K., H.Y., T.Y., X.Y., E.Y., K.M. and K.O. measured the content of DIMBOA. C.Z. and C.X. performed the <i>P. oryzae</i> experiment. Y.L., H.Y., D.C., C.-H.K., L.G., M.T., Q.Q. and L.B. discussed the data. L.F., J.Q. and M.T. wrote the paper.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to

C. <i>et al.</i> 
                     <i>Echinochloa crus-galli</i> genome analysis provides insight into its adaptation and invasiveness as a weed.
                    <i>Nat Commun</i> <b>8, </b>1031 (2017). https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-017-01067-5</p><p class="c-bibliographic-information__download-citation u-hide-print"><a data-test="citation-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="download article citation" data-track-label="link" data-track-external="" href="/articles/s41467-017-01067-5.ris">Download citation<svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-download"></use></svg></a></p><ul class="c-bibliographic-information__list" data-test="publication-history"><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Received<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2016-12-15">15 December 2016</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Accepted<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2017-08-16">16 August 2017</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Published<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2017-10-18">18 October 2017</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item c-bibliographic-information__list-item--doi"><p><abbr title="Digital Object Identifier">DOI</abbr><span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-017-01067-5" data-track="click" data-track-action="view doi" data-track-label="link" itemprop="sameAs">https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-017-01067-5</a></span></p></li></ul><div data-component="share-box"></div><div data-component="article-info-list"></div></div></div></div></div></section>
